User Code (Triggering the Issue)\n```python\nimport pandas as pd\nimport numpy as np\nfrom sklearn.preprocessing import StandardScaler\n\n# Create DataFrame with nullable integers and missing values\ndf = pd.DataFrame({\n    'col1': pd.array([1, 2, None, 4], dtype='Int64'),\n    'col2': pd.array([5, None, 7, 8], dtype='Int64')\n})\n\n# This will fail\nscaler = StandardScaler()\nscaler.fit(df)  # ValueError: \"cannot convert NA to integer\"\n```\n\n### 2. Entry Point: sklearn Preprocessing\n**File:** `sklearn/preprocessing/_data.py`\n- Functions like `StandardScaler.fit()` and `MinMaxScaler.fit()` accept pandas DataFrames\n- They call `validate_data()` to validate and normalize input\n\n### 3. Nullable integers ALWAYS require early conversion\n    return False\n```\n\n**Result:** Returns `True` for `Int64Dtype`, `Int32Dtype`, etc.\n\n#### Step 4c: Trigger Early Conversion\n**Lines 935-942:** Since `pandas_requires_conversion` is `True`, `check_array()` attempts early conversion:\n\n```python\nif pandas_requires_conversion:\n    # pandas dataframe requires conversion earlier to handle extension dtypes with nans\n    # Use the original dtype for conversion if dtype is None\n    new_dtype = dtype_orig if dtype is None else dtype\n    array = array.astype(new_dtype)  # Line 940 - FAILS HERE\n    # *** ROOT CAUSE ENDS HERE ***\n\n    if dtype.kind == \"b\" and self._hasna:\n        raise ValueError(\"cannot convert float NaN to bool\")\n\n    data = self.to_numpy(dtype=dtype, na_value=na_value, copy=copy)\n    return data\n```\n\n### Why This Check Exists\n\nThe check at line 683-684 is intentionally strict:\n- NumPy's integer dtypes cannot represent missing values natively\n- Unlike float dtypes which have `np.nan`, or object dtypes which can hold any Python object, integer arrays cannot represent missing data\n- The pandas library explicitly prevents this conversion to avoid silent data loss or unexpected behavior\n\n### The Problematic Scenario\n\nWhen `BaseMaskedArray.astype()` is called:\n1. `dtype` is `np.dtype('int64')` (or similar integer type)\n2. `dtype.kind` is `'i'` (integer kind)\n3. `self._hasna` is `True` (the array contains missing values)\n4. **Result:** ValueError is raised immediately, without attempting conversion\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow Through to_numpy() (Unused Path)\n\nAlthough unreachable when NA values exist, the `to_numpy()` method (Lines 512-607) also has safeguards:\n\n```python\ndef to_numpy(self, dtype: npt.DTypeLike | None = None, ...):\n    hasna = self._hasna\n    dtype, na_value = to_numpy_dtype_inference(self, dtype, na_value, hasna)\n\n    if hasna:\n        if (\n            dtype != np.dtype(object)\n            and not is_string_dtype(dtype)\n            and na_value is libmissing.NA\n        ):\n            # Lines 589-592: Raise if trying to convert to non-object dtype with NA values\n            raise ValueError(\n                f\"cannot convert to '{dtype}'-dtype NumPy array \"\n                \"with missing values. Specify an appropriate 'na_value' \"\n                \"for this dtype.\"\n            )\n```\n\nThis prevents accidental loss of NA values during conversion.\n\n---\n\n## Impact Chain\n\nThe error propagates through the call stack:\n\n```\nDataFrame.astype(dtype)\n  └─> Column[Int64Dtype].astype(dtype)\n      └─> BaseMaskedArray.astype(dtype)  ← ERROR RAISED HERE (Line 684)\n          └─> ValueError(\"cannot convert NA to integer\")\n\nStandardScaler.fit(df)\n  └─> validate_data(X, ...)\n      └─> check_array(X, dtype=np.float64, ...)\n          └─> array.astype(new_dtype)  ← Calls DataFrame.astype()\n              └─> ERROR PROPAGATES UP\n```\n\n---\n\n## Incompatibility Summary\n\n| Component | File | Issue |\n|-----------|------|-------|\n| **scikit-learn** | `sklearn/utils/validation.py:681-717` | `_pandas_dtype_needs_early_conversion()` identifies nullable integers as requiring early conversion |\n| **scikit-learn** | `sklearn/utils/validation.py:935-942` | `check_array()` attempts `.astype()` conversion before checking for missing values |\n| **pandas (ROOT CAUSE)** | `pandas/core/arrays/masked.py:683-684` | `BaseMaskedArray.astype()` explicitly rejects conversion of integer-typed nullable arrays to numpy integer dtypes when NA values are present |\n| **NumPy** | `numpy/_core/_methods.py` | Integer dtypes have no native missing value representation, preventing direct conversion |\n\n---\n\n## Specific Code Locations\n\n### Primary Root Cause\n- **File:** `pandas/core/arrays/masked.py`\n- **Function:** `BaseMaskedArray.astype()`\n- **Lines:** 683-684\n- **Code:**\n  ```python\n  if dtype.kind in \"iu\" and self._hasna:\n      raise ValueError(\"cannot convert NA to integer\")\n  ```\n\n### Secondary Contributing Factor\n- **File:** `sklearn/utils/validation.py`\n- **Function:** `_pandas_dtype_needs_early_conversion()`\n- **Lines:** 713-715\n- **Code:**\n  ```python\n  elif is_integer_dtype(pd_dtype):\n      # Triggers the error\n  ```\n\n---\n\n## Why This Is a Cross-Repository Problem\n\nThe incompatibility exists at the boundary between three major libraries:\n\n1. **NumPy** - No native support for missing values in integer arrays\n2. **pandas** - Nullable integer types (`Int64Dtype`) to support missing values, but prevents conversion to numpy integer dtypes\n3. **scikit-learn** - Expects to validate and convert numeric data to standard numpy arrays with explicit dtypes\n\nThe safe design in pandas (preventing silent data loss) conflicts with scikit-learn's expectation that numeric-looking data can be converted to numeric numpy arrays.\n\n---\n\n## Resolution Strategies (Not Implemented)\n\nPotential solutions would require cross-library coordination:\n\n1. **scikit-learn:** Skip early conversion for DataFrames with nullable dtypes\n2. **scikit-learn:** Use `.to_numpy(na_value=...)` instead of `.astype()` for nullable types\n3. **pandas:** Provide a way to convert nullable integers to float (since float can represent NaN)\n4. **pandas:** Allow conversion with an explicit NA placeholder value specified by the user\n\nHowever, these solutions involve design decisions that affect all three libraries and are outside the scope of simple bug fixes.\n\n---\n\n## Test Case\n\n```python\nimport pandas as pd\nimport numpy as np\nfrom sklearn.preprocessing import StandardScaler\n\n# Minimal reproducible example\ndf = pd.DataFrame({\n    'col': pd.array([1, 2, None], dtype='Int64')\n})\n\nscaler = StandardScaler()\ntry:\n    scaler.fit(df)\n    print(\"SUCCESS: No error\")\nexcept ValueError as e:\n    print(f\"ERROR: {e}\")\n    print(\"This error occurs because:\")\n    print(\"  1. sklearn's check_array() identifies Int64Dtype as needing conversion\")\n    print(\"  2.
